{{Italic title}}
{{Use dmy dates|date=March 2017}}
{{about|the official record of debates in the New Zealand Parliament, commonly called "Hansard"|the parliamentary records of other Commonwealth countries|Hansard}}
'''''Parliamentary Debates (Hansard)''''' is the official name of the transcripts of debates in the [[New Zealand Parliament]]. New Zealand was one of the first countries to establish an independent team of ''Hansard'' reporters,<ref>[http://www.history.net.nz/politics/history-of-parliament/reporting-and-broadcasting Parliaments' People, NZHistory site, NZ Ministry for Culture & Heritage]</ref> 42 years before the [[Parliament of the United Kingdom|British (Imperial) Parliament]]. An official record of debates has been kept continuously since 9 July 1867. Speeches made in the [[New Zealand House of Representatives|House of Representatives]] and the [[New Zealand Legislative Council|Legislative Council]] between 1867 and the commencement of Parliament in 1854 were compiled in 1885 from earlier newspaper reports, and this compilation also forms part of the New Zealand ''Hansard'' record.

The ''Hansard'' takes its name from [[Thomas Curson Hansard]], who started publishing a daily record of proceedings in the British Parliament in the early 19th century.<ref>{{cite web |title=What is Hansard? |url=https://www.parliament.nz/en/pb/hansard-debates/what-is-hansard/ |publisher=New Zealand Parliament |accessdate=11 December 2018 |language=en}}</ref>

==History==
[[File:Cartoon_about_NZ_Parliamentary_Debates_from_NZ_Observer_12_October_1895.jpg|right|upright=1.5|NZ Observer & Free Lance 1895]]
For 13 years from the establishment of the New Zealand Parliament in [[Auckland]] in 1854 newspaper reports were the only record of what MPs said in debates in the [[New Zealand Legislative Council|Legislative Council]] and the [[New Zealand House of Representatives|House of Representatives]]. The accuracy of these reports often depended on the political leanings of the owners of the newspaper in which they were published, and consistency of reporting was a real problem,<ref name="25th anniversary">[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/EP19310416.2.46? Evening Post, 16 April 1931, page 11]</ref> as noted in an article in the ''Wellington Independent'' newspaper in 1860:<ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/WI18601009.2.11 Wellington Independent, 9 October 1860, page 3]</ref>
<blockquote>“''These reports give you little notion of the reality. Some members … whose speeches are dreary beyond belief, and almost unintelligible as delivered in the House, [become] flowing oratory in the columns of the newspaper.  While others… are shorn of their fair proportions, and their speeches reduced to mere notes… Members who usually talk to empty benches [appear] as prominent as those who electrify the gallery or are the life of the House.''”</blockquote>

[[MPs|MP]] [[William Fitzherbert (New Zealand politician)|William Fitzherbert]] brought a motion to the House in 1856 calling for funds to be applied to "''secure accurate and authentic reports of the substance and arguments of the speeches''".<ref name="12 June 1856">[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740189;view=1up;seq=202 ''Parliamentary Debates 1856–1858'', 12 June 1856, page 152]</ref> Then in 1862 [[James FitzGerald (New Zealand politician)|James FitzGerald]] ([[MPs|MP]] for Christchurch and owner of ''[[The Press]]'') introduced a motion calling on the Government to take steps to secure the publication of "''full and accurate reports of the debates in this House''".<ref name="25 August 1862">[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740205;view=1up;seq=672 ''Parliamentary Debates 1861–1863'', 25 August 1862, page 606]</ref>  Despite both motions being unanimously agreed, it was not until 1866 that a Select Committee, chaired by [[James FitzGerald (New Zealand politician)|FitzGerald]], was established to “''consider and report as to the best manner in which the debates of the General Assembly can be reported and printed''.”<ref name="5 July 1866">[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740213;view=1up;seq=833 ''Parliamentary Debates 1864–1866'', 5 July 1866, page 761]</ref>

On 9 July 1867 a team of five reporters (AJ Dallas, George McIntyre, James Kinsella, ET Gillon, and William Mitchell who later drowned<ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/AS18980624.2.54 Auckland Star, 24 June 1898, page 5]</ref>),<ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/DSC18671014.2.26? Daily Southern Cross 14 October 1867, page 4]</ref><ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/NZH18920712.2.30 New Zealand Herald, 12 July 1892, page 5]</ref><ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/NZH18840325.2.18 New Zealand Herald, 25 March 1884, page 5]</ref> led by Chief Reporter [[C.C.N. Barron]], produced the first official report of debates of the New Zealand Parliament.<ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/EP18920711.2.10 [[The Evening Post (New Zealand)|Evening Post]], 11 July 1892, page 2]</ref><ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/EP18880709.2.8 [[The Evening Post (New Zealand)|Evening Post]], 9 July 1888, page 2]</ref> One notable ''Hansard'' Reporter from the 1870s and 1880s was [[George Fisher (New Zealand politician)|George Fisher]], who was mayor of [[Wellington]] for four terms, member of Parliament for Wellington and Minister of Education and Commissioner of Trade and Customs.<ref name="25th anniversary"/><ref name ="shorthand">[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/ODT18840403.2.36 Otago Daily Times, 3 April 1884, page 4]</ref> Another notable early ''Hansard'' Reporter was Charles Melville Crombie, who later became Chief Commissioner of Taxes.<ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/EP18940607.2.11 Evening Post, 7 June 1894, page 2]</ref>

[[File:Cartoon_about_NZ_Parliamentary_Debates_from_NZ_Observer_25_Aug._1894.jpg|upright=1.5|right|NZ Observer & Free Lance 1894]]
Reporters worked in 15 minute "turns" and had to cover speeches in both debating chambers, regularly working until after midnight to finish the day's reports, taking notes using [[Pitman shorthand]] and then transcribing these by dictation.<ref name ="shorthand"/> From the establishment of the ''Hansard'' team speeches were reported as fully as possible, although for many years it was regularly proposed that only summaries of speeches should be published.<ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/EP18880709.2.8? Evening Post, 9 July 1888, page 2]</ref> Reporters had to cope with speakers who had a variety of different accents and speaking pace, and had to learn the names of an increasing number of members, with the [[New Zealand House of Representatives#Number of members|number of members]] in the House alone increasing from 37 in 1854 to 95 by 1882. Competent reporters with [[shorthand]] skills were scarce in New Zealand and men were brought in during parliamentary sessions from Australian parliaments to assist local reporters.

In 1884 Maurice FitzGerald, son of [[James FitzGerald (New Zealand politician)|James FitzGerald]], was engaged to compile from newspaper reports speeches made in Parliament between 1854 and 1867.<ref>[http://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/EP18841108.2.12 Evening Post, 8 November 1884, page 2]</ref><ref>[http://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/HBH18841110.2.12.1 Hawke's Bay Herald, 10 November 1884, page 3]</ref><ref>[http://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/THD18841110.2.13 Timaru Herald, 10 November 1884, page 2]</ref><ref>[http://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/HBH18841111.2.10? Hawke's Bay Herald, 11 November 1884, page 3]</ref> Maurice Fitzgerald completed this work in 1885.<ref>Letter from Maurice FitzGerald to [[Prime Minister of New Zealand|Premier]] [[Robert Stout]] 22 August 1885, Archives NZ reference R24418249</ref><ref>[http://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/TAN18860424.2.28 Te Aroha News, 24 April 1886, page 5]</ref> He died in 1886 (at 25 years of age) from [[tuberculosis]]<ref>[http://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/EP18860710.2.13 Evening Post, 10 July 1886, page 2]</ref> before all five volumes of his compilation were printed.<ref name="Postscript">[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740213;view=1up;seq=1127 ''Parliamentary Debates 1864–1866'', Postscript, page 1055]</ref><ref>[http://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/EP18860720.2.12 Evening Post, 20 July 1886, page 2]</ref>

==New Zealand ''Hansard'' today==
Official transcripts of [[MPs]]' speeches in the House have been continuously published since 1867. Today ''Hansard'' is produced by a team of about 17 [[Full-time equivalent|FTE]] Hansard editors within the [[Office of the Clerk of the House of Representatives]].{{citation needed|date=December 2018}} ''Hansard'' is published on the New Zealand Parliament website each day the House sits, and later indexed bound volumes are produced.

Speeches are transcribed directly from digital recordings of the debate, with staff present in the [[debating chamber]] to monitor the debate by recording the sequence of speakers and any interjections. Interjections are reported only if the member speaking replies to them or remarks on them during the course of his or her speech. Hansard Editors follow strict rules on what changes they can make to the words MPs use in the debating chamber. ''Hansard'' is as close to [[wikt:verbatim|verbatim]] as possible, although Hansard Editors remove repetitions and redundancies and make minor grammatical corrections. MPs are provided draft copies of their speeches at the same time that the speeches are first published on the Parliament website. MPs can request correction of inadvertent factual inaccuracies but they are unable to significantly change what they said in the House.<ref>[https://www.parliament.nz/en/pb/hansard-debates/what-is-hansard/ New Zealand Parliament website, "What is Hansard?", Retrieved 13 September 2016]</ref><ref>[https://www.parliament.nz/en/get-involved/features-pre-2016/document/00NZPHomeNews270420091/650th-bound-edition-of-hansard-published New Zealand Parliament website, "650th bound edition of Hansard published", Retrieved 13 September 2016]</ref>
{{clear}}

==Timeline of establishment of ''Hansard'' in New Zealand==
{| class="wikitable"
|-
! Date
! Event or decision relevant to reporting of debates
|-
|24 May 1854
|The General Assembly sat for the first time, with an upper house, the Legislative Council, consisting of 12 appointed Legislative Councillors, and a House of Representatives consisting of 37<ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/NZSCSG18530312.2.8 Proclamation from Government Gazette of 10 March 1853, New Zealand Spectator and Cook's Strait Guardian, 12 March 1853, page 3]</ref> elected Members of the House.
|-
|May/June 1854
|A "reporting club" of MPs was formed, consisting of [[James FitzGerald (New Zealand politician)|James FitzGerald]], [[Henry Sewell]], [[Edward Gibbon Wakefield]], [[Jerningham Wakefield|Edward Jerningham Wakefield]], [[James Macandrew]], [[Hugh Carleton]] and [[William Cutten]]. Because of the lack of press reporters with [[shorthand]] skills this group undertook to take notes of speeches in the House, which would then be provided to each member who had spoken for checking, before being provided to newspapers for publication.<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740171;view=1up;seq=230 ''Parliamentary Debates 1854–1855'', 7 July 1854, page 184]</ref><ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/DSC18540919.2.9 The Southern Cross, 19 September 1854, page 3]</ref> The collegiality of members of the reporting club was short-lived: by early July Henry Sewell complained that Edward Gibbon Wakefield "''does not scruple here and there to doctor and color what has been really said, not absolutely falsifying, and yet giving slight touches which wholly alter the real character... his speeches are embellished throughout with cheers, as if the House sympathized heartily''".<ref>{{cite book|ref = JHS |last = Sewell|first = Henry|title = The Journal of Henry Sewell 1853–7 : Volume 2|year = 1980|publisher = Whitcoulls Publishers|location = Christchurch|isbn = 0723306230|authorlink = Henry Sewell|editor = W. David McIntyre|page = 54}}</ref>
|-
|12 June 1856
|MPs agreed a motion moved by [[William Fitzherbert (New Zealand politician)|William Fitzherbert]] calling for funds to be applied to "''secure accurate and authentic reports of the substance and arguments of the speeches made by honorable{{sic}} members of the House''"<ref name="12 June 1856"/>
|-
|25 August 1862
|MPs agreed a motion moved by James FitzGerald calling on the Government to take steps to secure the publication of "''full and accurate reports of the debates in this House''"<ref name="25 August 1862"/>
|-
|2 December 1863
|MPs reaffirm the motion moved by James FitzGerald calling on the Government to take steps to secure the publication of "''full and accurate reports of the debates in this House''"<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740205;view=1up;seq=1039''Parliamentary Debates 1861–1863'', 2 December 1863, page 973]</ref> 
|-
|8 & 14 August 1865
|MPs agreed a motion moved by [[Frederick Weld]]: "''That a Select Committee be appointed to superintend the revision of the reports of debates''"<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740213;view=1up;seq=329 ''Parliamentary Debates 1864–1866'', 8 August 1865, page 257]</ref> A similar motion moved by [[James Crowe Richmond]] was passed in the [[New Zealand Legislative Council|Legislative Council]]<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740213;view=1up;seq=370 ''Parliamentary Debates 1864–1866'', 14 August 1865, page 298]</ref>
|-
|5 & 17 July 1866
|MPs agreed a motion moved by [[Edward Stafford (politician)|Edward Stafford]]  "''That a Select Committee be appointed to consider and report as to the best manner in which the debates of the General Assembly can be reported and printed.''"<ref name="5 July 1866"/> This Committee reported to the House that the Government should eventually "''engage a staff of competent reporters''" but until that could be done the [[Wellington]] newspapers should be paid to "''furnish full and accurate reports daily of the proceedings in both Houses.''"<ref>[https://www.atojs.natlib.govt.nz/cgi-bin/atojs?a=d&cl=search&d=AJHR1866-I.2.1.7.3&srpos=69&e=-------100--1---bySH---0-AJHR%5f1866%5fI%5fAZz-G- ''Appendix to the Journals of the House of Representatives'', 1866 Session I, F-03, 13 July 1866]</ref><ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/DSC18660730.2.25 Daily Southern Cross, 30 July 1866, page 4]</ref><ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/EP18660713.2.7 Evening Post, 13 July 1866, page 2]</ref> However the House refused to agree a resolution moved by Committee Chairman James FitzGerald to enter into a contract with local newspaper proprietors, as had been proposed by the report.<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740213;view=1up;seq=853 ''Parliamentary Debates 1864–1866'', 17 July 1866, page 781]</ref><ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/CHP18660721.2.13? ''[[The Press]]'', 21 July 1866, page 2]</ref><ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/WI18660719.2.17.2 Wellington Independent, 19 July 1866, page 6]</ref>
|-
|26 July 1866
|James FitzGerald drew the House's attention to the fact that newspapers were deliberately omitting to report the speeches, or even the name, of a certain member. A note in ''Hansard'' indicates that FitzGerald was referring to the Wellington newspapers purposely omitting any mention of [[Dillon Bell|Francis Dillon Bell]].<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740213;view=1up;seq=889 ''Parliamentary Debates 1864–1866'', 26 July 1866, page 817]</ref>
|-
|28 September 1866
|Thomas MacKenzie, proprietor of the ''Wellington Independent'' newspaper was summoned to appear before the House for a "''breach of [[Parliamentary Privilege|Privilege]]''" by publishing a report of parliamentary debates that indicated that [[Arthur John Burns]] (Member for [[Caversham (New Zealand electorate)|Caversham]]) had acted [[Malice (law)|maliciously]] by raising a certain matter in House.<ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/NZH18661008.2.27? New Zealand Herald, 8 October 1866, page 5]</ref><ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/WI18661016.2.16 Wellington Independent, 16 October 1866, page 6]</ref><ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/WI18661002.2.13 Wellington Independent, 2 October 1866, page 5]</ref>
|-
|9 July 1867
|[[C.C.N. Barron|Clarke Charles Netterville Barron]] is appointed as Chief Reporter and tasked with establishing a team of reporters to record debates in both Houses of Parliament.
<ref>[https://www.atojs.natlib.govt.nz/cgi-bin/atojs?a=d&cl=search&d=AJHR1868-I.2.1.5.14&srpos=65&e=-------100--1---bySH---0-AJHR%5f1868%5fI%5fAZz-F- ''Appendix to the Journals of the House of Representatives'', 1868 Session I, D-13, 1 July 1868]</ref>
|-
|10 July 1867
|[[Colonial Secretary (New Zealand)|Colonial Secretary]] [[Edward Stafford (politician)|Edward Stafford]] advised the House that the Government had established "''a reporting staff of four persons, and a head of the staff, who will take down and report the proceedings of both Houses, which will be printed''". A Select Committee was appointed to "''have entire control over the reporting''"... this was an "''experiment''"; the Select "''Committee was to ascertain whether the present arrangements could be improved.''"<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740221;view=1up;seq=63 ''Parliamentary Debates Volume 1.1'', 10 July 1867, pages 16–22]</ref> The ''Wellington Independent'' derided the government's decision to establish a team of ''Hansard'' reporters, rather than enter into a contract with local newspapers to report on debates.<ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/WI18670611.2.10 Wellington Independent, 11 June 1867, page 3]</ref><ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/WI18670615.2.30 Wellington Independent, 15 June 1867, page 7]</ref>
|-
|16 July 1867
|The Select Committee on Reporting Debates adopted rules that allowed Members "''the opportunity of revising reports, on the strict understanding that the alterations are to be confined to making the reports more in accordance with the remarks actually uttered in the House. The head reporter to be the judge of the alterations made, and to refuse to pass those which he considers are departures from a correct report of what the speaker said.''"<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740221;view=1up;seq=102 ''Parliamentary Debates Volume 1.1'', 16 July 1867, page 56]</ref>
|-
|6 August 1868
|After lengthy debate, the House refused to agree a resolution moved by [[Charles Heaphy]] that "''having in view the burdensome taxation of the country... the present system of reporting the debates, and the expense thereof, should cease with the termination of existing contracts.''"<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740239;view=1up;seq=337 ''Parliamentary Debates Volume 2'', 6 August 1868, page 311]</ref> 
|-
|1 September 1869
|A Reporting Debates Committee appointed by the House on 4 June 1869 "''for the purpose of regulating the proceedings of the reporters, and endeavouring to provide for the better compilation of the reports''"<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740270;view=1up;seq=56 ''Parliamentary Debates Volume 5'', 4 June 1869, page 32]</ref> reaffirmed the rule established by the 1867 Select Committee on Reporting Debates that if Members seek to make material alterations in the reports of their speeches the '''Chief Reporter should have the power to refuse to pass such corrections to the Printer''".<ref>[https://www.atojs.natlib.govt.nz/cgi-bin/atojs?a=d&d=AJHR1869-I.2.2.6.9&srpos=65&e=-------10--1------0-- ''Appendix to the Journals of the House of Representatives'', 1869 Session I, F-08, 30 August 1869]</ref>
|-
|14 July 1870
|The Reporting Debates Committee considered, but did not agree to, a proposal by [[John Davies Ormond]] (Member for [[Clive (New Zealand electorate)|Clive]]) that ''"Hansard staff should be required to prepare summaries of the debates in the House for transmission by telegraph to the various newspapers of the colony"''.<ref>[https://paperspast.natlib.govt.nz/newspapers/HBT18700725.2.11? Hawke's Bay Times, 25 July 1870, page 4]</ref>
|-
|14 November 1871
|MPs agreed a motion moved by [[William Henry Harrison (New Zealand politician)|William Harrison]]: "''That, with the view to improving the character of Hansard, a permanent staff of efficient reporters should be engaged for that service,''" (at that time most reporters were employed on a sessional basis) "''and that it should be a primary duty of the Chief Reporter to take his share in the task of reporting.''" (The Chief Reporter was currently mostly doing administration and checking reports, rather than reporting.)<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740320;view=1up;seq=1123 ''Parliamentary Debates Volume 11'', 14 November 1871, pages 1077–1079]</ref> 
|-
|24 September & 25 October 1872
|MPs noted a marked improvement in ''[[Hansard]]'' due to the appointment of permanent reporters<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740346;view=1up;seq=345''Parliamentary Debates Volume 13'', 24 September 1872, pages 304–305]</ref><ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740346;view=1up;seq=986 ''Parliamentary Debates Volume 13'', 25 October 1872, page 946]</ref>
|-
|28 July 1875
|After lengthy debate, the House refused to agree a proposal from the Reporting Debates Committee that "''Hansard reporters be directed to report "short" those debates which are not of general public interest.''" This proposal would have seen many speeches reported in a précis format, with only "''matters of political importance... reported as nearly as possible in extenso''".<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019787149;view=1up;seq=101 ''Parliamentary Debates Volume 17'', 28 July 1875, pages 73 – 76]</ref>
|-
|8 August 1879
|MPs again rejected a proposal brought by the Reporting Debates and Printing Committee that would have allowed the Chief Reporter "''the exercise of a discretionary power as to reporting matters arising incidentally in the House, and not set down as business of the day'' [because] ''with the limited staff at his disposal, it was impossible... to report everything that took place in the House''".<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019787271;view=1up;seq=528 ''Parliamentary Debates Volume 31'', 8 August 1879, page 505]</ref>
|-
|3 December 1879
|MPs again rejected a proposal brought by the Reporting Debates committees of both houses "''that the debates published in Hansard shall be condensed next session''".<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019787313;view=1up;seq=141 ''Parliamentary Debates Volume 34'', 3 December 1879, page 639]</ref>
|-
|7 July 1880
|MPs agreed a motion "''that it be an instruction to the Printing and Debates Committee to inquire into and report to this House in what manner retrenchment can best be effected in the cost of the publication of Hansard.''"<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019787321;view=1up;seq=84''Parliamentary Debates Volume 36'', 7 July 1880, page 54]</ref>
|-
|15 June 1882
|MPs rejected a motion "''that members shall defray the cost of printing their own speeches in Hansard; and that such cost shall be deducted from the honorarium, if any, to which they may be entitled''". (If it had been passed this motion would have allowed members to choose whether or not their speeches were reported in ''Hansard''.)''".<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019787362;view=1up;seq=507 ''Parliamentary Debates Volume 41'', 15 June 1882, page 471]</ref>
|-
|7 November 1884
|[[William Steward (New Zealand politician)|William Steward]] advised the House that the Reporting Debates and Printing Committee had sanctioned the ordering of four 'Caligraph' typewriters as a trial ''"with a view to adding to the facilities of the reporting staff"''.<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019787453;view=1up;seq=500 ''Parliamentary Debates Volume 50'', 8 November 1884, page 470]</ref>
|-
|8 November 1884
|[[Prime Minister of New Zealand|Premier]] [[Robert Stout]] advised the House that Maurice FitzGerald, son of James FitzGerald, would be engaged to compile from newspaper reports speeches made in Parliament between 1854 and 1867.<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019787453;view=1up;seq=526 ''Parliamentary Debates Volume 50'', 8 November 1884, page 496]</ref> This work was completed the following year but the last of the five volume compilation was not printed until 1887.<ref name="Postscript"/>
|}

==Volumes==
''Hansard'' has been digitized by [[Google Books#Google Books Library Project|Google]] in partnership with the [[University of California]] ([[University of California Libraries#Santa Cruz|Santa Cruz et al. libraries]]), from the first sitting of the [[New Zealand House of Representatives|House]] in May 1854 up to July 1987.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.parliament.nz/en/pb/hansard-debates/for-the-record-150-years-of-hansard/hansard-goes-digital-to-celebrate-its-150th-anniversary/|title=Hansard goes digital to celebrate its 150th anniversary - New Zealand Parliament|website=www.parliament.nz|language=en|access-date=2019-05-22}}</ref> These digital volumes are hosted by [[HathiTrust]] and are available via the links in the first column of the table below. The entire collection up to July 1987 is searchable using the [[HathiTrust]] [https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/mb?a=listis&c=71329709 website]. The last column of the table below has links to other digital volumes created in partnership with university libraries if these are publicly available via [[HathiTrust]].

''Hansard'' from 16 September 1987 to 17 December 2002 created from word processing files (i.e., not the official printed volumes) is available via the links in the first column of the table below and the 123 volumes in this period can be downloaded [https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/0B1Iwfzv-Mt3CRGZkMWNfeXoybmc?usp=sharing here] (this is useful for searching across the collection).

''Hansard'' from 11 February 2003 onwards is available from the [[Parliament of New Zealand|NZ Parliament]] [https://www.parliament.nz/en/pb/hansard-debates/ website]. The period 11 February 2003 to 9 June 2016 is also available via the links in the first column of the table below and the 109 volumes in this period can be downloaded [https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/0B1Iwfzv-Mt3CWWN5ZVEyQVYyNWM?usp=sharing here].

| class="toccolours" |'''Volume notes'''
<sup id="volumenote1">1</sup>1854–1866 volumes were compiled by Maurice FitzGerald in 1885 from earlier newspaper reports.<ref>[https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=uc1.32106019740171;view=1up;seq=9 Preface to ''Parliamentary Debates 1854–1855'']</ref>

<sup id="volumenote2">2</sup> In 1867 the first official [[New Zealand]] ''[[Hansard]]'' was compiled by reporters employed on a sessional basis.

<sup id="volumenote3">3</sup> Volume 1.2 includes an appendix of financial data for various years.

<sup id="volumenote4">4</sup> Volume 146 includes a 61-page appendix: Proceedings of the meetings of both Houses (held 7 June 1909) to discuss the question of representation of NZ at the Imperial Naval Conference.

<sup id="volumenote7">7</sup> Volume 316 is the first volume to use the title Parliamentary Debates ''(Hansard)''.

<sup id="volumenote8">8</sup> This digitised volume 326 is missing pages 1 to 128 (20 to 28 June 1961).

<sup id="volumenote9">9</sup> Volume digitized in partnership with the [[University of Chicago]].

<sup id="volumenote10">10</sup> Volume digitized in partnership with [[Harvard University]].

<sup id="volumenote11">11</sup> Volume digitized in partnership with the [[University of California]] ([[University of California Libraries#Los Angeles (13 major libraries—including Law and Medical)|Los Angeles et al. libraries]]).

<sup id="volumenote12">12</sup> Volume digitized in partnership with the [[University of Illinois at Urbana–Champaign]].

<sup id="volumenote13">13</sup> Volume digitized in partnership with the [[University of Michigan]].
|}
